How it works. And how you can use it for amazing results.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Specifically, by applying the rule of space to photography, you can embrace the quieter moments in visual imagery &#8211; and you can amplify the impact of your subject by balancing positive and negative <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/5-elements-of-composition-in-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"compositional elements (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">compositional elements</a>.  </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let&#8217;s dive right in.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image data-section id=\"what-is-the-rule-of-space-in-photography\">What is the rule of space in photography?</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The rule of space in photography is a method of incorporating visual absence to give a subject <em>room to breathe</em>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Although the rule of space is more like a guide than a rigid rule, it is a handy compositional device. It&#8217;s a great way to add a sense of vastness, <a aria-label=\"depth (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/depth-dimension-photos/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">depth</a>, and/or motion to a photograph. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"why-is-the-rule-of-space-important\">Why is the rule of space important?</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>To understand the rule of space, we first need to take a brief look at positive and negative space. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Photographers use the terms <em>positive space</em> and <a aria-label=\"negative space (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/negative-space-in-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\"><em>negative</em> <em>space</em></a> to contrast impactful and more subtle areas in a photograph. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Generally, positive space refers to specific subjects that command a viewer&#8217;s attention. Negative space, on the other hand, is less visually demanding and provides a frame for the main event in an image. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, in the image below, the clouds represent positive space, whereas the sky and dark shadows create the negative space that frames the main subject:  </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202477\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:66.67%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" photography clouds\" class=\"wp-image-202477\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_clouds_kennedy.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption><a href=\"https://geni.us/CanonEOS5DMarkIV\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Canon 5D Mark IV (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Canon 5D Mark IV</a> | <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/writers-favorite-lens-the-canon-24-105mm-f4/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Canon EF 24-105mm f/4L IS USM (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Canon EF 24-105mm f/4L IS USM</a> | f/10 | 1/500s | ISO 100</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>So where does the rule of space in photography fit in? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>In general terms, the rule of space governs the use of negative space within an image. By understanding the nature of the rule of space, a photographer can harness the intent of a subject, as well as add depth and perspective to the image. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The rule of space is important because it aids a photographer in articulating the energy of a photograph &#8211; and it guides the viewer&#8217;s eye by sculpting key visual events and affording the subject more room to move.   </p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"working-with-the-rule-of-space-the-basics\">Working with the rule of space: the basics</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>To work with the rule of space in photography, first consider the behavior of your subject. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Ask yourself: What is the subject doing? Is it moving or stationary? How does it occupy space? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>At the same time, visualize what you want to convey in the photograph. Is it movement? Perspective? Depth? Narrative? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The nature and behavior of your subject plus your intent should together determine how you apply the rule of space.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"perspective\">Perspective </h3>\n\n\n\n<p>One of the main ways the rule of space can impact a photograph is through <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/perspective-photography-dont-just-stand-move-feet/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">perspective</a>. Abundant space around a subject can make the subject appear smaller or larger depending on the <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/make-photos-creative-using-camera-angles/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"camera angle (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">camera angle</a>.  </p>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, a subject photographed from a high angle, surrounded with minimal detail, can seem smaller and more immersed in negative space: </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202556\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:66.67%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_cat_window_kennedy.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>Canon 5D Mark IV | <a href=\"https://geni.us/Canon24-105\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Canon EF 24-105mm f/4L IS USM (opens in a new tab)\" id=\"conveying-momentum\">Conveying momentum</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>The rule of space in photography can help you create the impression of movement. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>To convey action, the rule suggests that space should be left either <em>in front of</em> or <em>behind </em>the subject (or both). </p>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, if a subject is moving across a scene, you can aim to capture both the subject and the negative space surrounding the subject. The extra space conveys the subject&#8217;s movement, adding the momentum a tight crop may lack.  </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202777\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:66.67%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_jet_star_flight_kennedy.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"airplane flying\" class=\"wp-image-202777\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_jet_star_flight_kennedy.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_jet_star_flight_kennedy.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_jet_star_flight_kennedy.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_jet_star_flight_kennedy.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_jet_star_flight_kennedy.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_jet_star_flight_kennedy.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>Allowing a subject room to move adds momentum. <br />Canon 5D Mark II | Canon EF 24-105mm f/4L IS USM | f/10 | 1/640s | ISO 250</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"adding-depth\">Adding depth </h3>\n\n\n\n<p>The rule of space in photography is not limited to highly active subjects; it works for stationary subject matter, too!</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, in portraiture, your composition can be governed by pairing the gaze or gesticulations of the subject with negative space. A subject&#8217;s gaze naturally directs our attention &#8211; we want to see what the subject sees. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>But when a gaze is met by negative space, the viewer&#8217;s eye will often naturally return to the original source of the gaze. The rule of space provides an organic way of adding depth and directing viewer attention. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can also use the rule of space with non-human/animal subject matter &#8211; based on their movement, perceived gesticulations, and extensions. By following the momentum, composition, or behavior of a non-human subject, you&#8217;ll find ideal placements for negative space. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>In the example below, I surrounded several blossoms with negative space; this additional room suggests growth and depth. It also highlights the detail in the individual florets. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202536\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:66.67%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" in photography\" class=\"wp-image-202536\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_pink_flowers_kennedy.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_pink_flowers_kennedy.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Canon EF 50mm f/1.8 II</a> with extension tubes | f/2.5 | 1/1250s | ISO 200</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"rule-of-space-challenges\">Rule of space challenges </h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The process of applying the rule of space to photographs is not that difficult in itself. However, a tendency to cram each image with as much visual information as possible can get in the way of exploring negative space. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Instead, deliberately and mindfully take a minimalist approach. You can also zoom out or physically take a few steps back from a subject to refocus on the rule of space. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"tips-and-techniques-for-working-with-the-rule-of-space\">Tips and techniques for working with the rule of space</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Here are a few tips for working with the rule of space:</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"tip-use-other-compositional-rules-too\">Tip 1: Use other compositional rules, too</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Applying the rule of space to your photography doesn&#8217;t have to come at the cost of other compositional rules. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>In fact, combining compositional tenets with the rule of space in photography can <em>increase </em>the chances of creating a successful photograph. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Compositional rules such as the <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/rule-of-thirds/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">rule of thirds</a>, <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-use-leading-lines-for-better-compositions/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">leading lines</a>, <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/understanding-depth-field-beginners/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">depth of field</a>, and <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/using-repetition-and-patterns-in-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">repetition</a> can all be used in conjunction with the rule of space to create engaging imagery.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202765\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:66.67%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_lightning_kennedy.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"lightning striking above a city\" class=\"wp-image-202765\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_lightning_kennedy.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_lightning_kennedy.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_lightning_kennedy.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_lightning_kennedy.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_lightning_kennedy.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_lightning_kennedy.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>Canon 5D Mark IV | Canon EF 24-105mm f/4L IS USM | f/5 | 30s | ISO 100</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"tip-let-it-breathe\">Tip 2: Let it breathe </h3>\n\n\n\n<p>The rule of space is all about giving a subject or a scene room to breathe. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>So step back, zoom out, or even try a wider lens; that way, you can add a sense of spaciousness to your photos. </p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"tip-experiment-with-different-camera-settings\">Tip 3: Experiment with different camera settings </h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Your choice of camera settings can help follow the rule of space more effectively. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>For instance, you might use a shallow depth of field to surround a subject with negative space. You could also try using a slow shutter speed and <a aria-label=\"pan your camera (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/mastering-panning-to-photograph-moving-subjects/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">panning your camera</a> while leaving space before or after a subject to amplify movement. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202780\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:66.67%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_fence_kennedy.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"fence with shallow depth of field rule of space in photography\" class=\"wp-image-202780\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_fence_kennedy.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_fence_kennedy.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_fence_kennedy.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_fence_kennedy.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/rule_of_space_in_photography_fence_kennedy.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/dps-writers-favorite-canon-100-400mm-lens/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Canon EF 100-400mm f/4.5-5.6L IS II USM (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Canon EF 100-400mm f/4.5-5.6L IS II USM</a> | f/5.6 | 1/125s | ISO 200</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"the-rule-of-space-in-photography-conclusion\">The rule of space in photography: conclusion</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The rule of space aims to create a mindful harmony of positive and negative space. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>And by applying this rule, you can emphasize and frame positive subject matter while generating an evocative balance of weight and weightlessness within an image.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So the next time you&#8217;re out with your camera, remember the rule of space &#8211; and do what you can to apply it in your images!</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now over to you:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>Have you been using the rule of space in your photos? How are you going to change your compositions to improve your use of space? Share your thoughts (and photos!) in the comments below.</em> </p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"rule-of-space-faqs\">Rule of spaceÂ FAQs</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"schema-faq wp-block-yoast-faq-block\"><div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1611013412226\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">What is the rule of space?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">In visual art, the rule of space guides your inclusion of negative space within an image. </p> </div> <div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1611185047241\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">What is negative space?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">Generally, negative space refers to areas in a photograph that are not occupied by the main subject matter. Often, negative space serves as a frame to emphasize the key subjects in an image. </p> </div> <div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1611013647506\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">How do photographers use the rule of space in composition?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">The rule encourages photographers to make use of negative space. There are many ways to do this. You can focus on coupling subjects with negative space by selecting minimalist backdrops, or you can pair the gaze of a portrait subject with additional negative space. </p> </div> <div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1611013998042\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">Who are some photographers that use the rule of space?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">There are countless photographers who make use of the rule of space. For example, photographers <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://www.martinparr.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Martin Parr</a> and <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://www.moma.org/artists/3520\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Helen Levitt</a> made striking use of the rule, as well as <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://www.sugimotohiroshi.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Hiroshi Sugimoto</a>, <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://www.michaelkenna.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Michael Kenna</a>, and <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://erickimphotography.com/blog/2018/06/28/minimalist-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Eric Kim</a>.</p> </div> <div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1611014727737\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">When can I break the rule of space in photography?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">Photography is all about developing personal creative instincts and approaches. That&#8217;s why compositional rules can be broken. The rule of space in photography is simply a guide &#8211; so if an image looks better without extra space, then go with your instincts. And if you aren&#8217;t sure, try taking a series of photos with different spatial approaches and analyze the results.</p> </div> </div>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/rule-of-space-in-photography/\">The Rule of Space in Photography: A Comprehensive Guide (+ Examples)</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>. data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Last week, <a href=\"https://pressroom.pixelshift.studio/sony-electronics-introduces-three-new-high-performance-g-lenses-to-its-full-frame-e-mount-lens-lineup\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Sony announced three E-mount lenses (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Sony announced three E-mount lenses</a>: </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The <a aria-label=\"FE 24mm f/2.8 G (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://geni.us/Sony24mmf2-8dPS\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">FE 24mm f/2.8 G</a>, the <a aria-label=\"FE 40mm f/2.5 G (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://geni.us/Sony40mmf2-5dPS\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">FE 40mm f/2.5 G</a>, and the <a aria-label=\"FE 50mm f/2.5 G (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://geni.us/Sony50mmf2-5dPS\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">FE 50mm f/2.5 G</a>; all promise to deliver excellent optics in a compact form.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The three lenses will launch this May. Designed as a set, they offer a beautifully wide field of view on the 24mm end for <a aria-label=\"scenic shots (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/11-surefire-tips-for-improving-your-landscape-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">scenic shots</a> and <a aria-label=\"environmental portraits (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/environmental-portraits/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">environmental portraits</a>, plus a standard perspective at the 40mm and 50mm focal lengths, perfect for <a aria-label=\"portraits (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/10-ways-to-take-stunning-portraits/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">portraits</a>, <a aria-label=\"street photography (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/ultimate-guide-street-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">street photography</a>, and even detail shots.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-206760\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; </p>\n\n\n\n<p>And while we can&#8217;t currently confirm the resolution of these lenses with a hands-on review of our own, sample images look <em>very </em>nice, and Sony&#8217;s own tests show tack-sharp results especially when stopped down to f/8. If you&#8217;re an APS-C shooter who demands the highest optical quality, or you&#8217;re working full frame and want some compact-yet-capable prime lenses, the 24mm f/2.8, 40mm f/2.5, and 50mm f/2.5 will deliver.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Plus, all three lenses offer fast maximum apertures, which translates to lovely <a aria-label=\"bokeh (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-achieve-nice-bokeh-in-plain-english/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">bokeh</a> &#8211; especially on the 50mm f/2.5, but also on the 40mm f/2.5 and even the 24mm f/2.8 when shooting close-ups.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Of course, f/2.5 and f/2.8 maximum apertures will get you more than just creamy backgrounds. With a <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/aperture/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"wide aperture (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">wide aperture</a>, you can shoot indoors or at twilight while still maintaining a reasonable <a aria-label=\"ISO (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/iso-settings/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">ISO</a>, so you can photograph <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/tips-event-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"events (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">events</a> and <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/create-shoot-night-portraits/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"night portraits (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">night portraits</a> &#8211; or record low-light video &#8211; and come away with clean results.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Sony also promises &#8220;fast, precise AF with excellent tracking performance&#8221; and top-notch build quality (all three lenses are dust and moisture resistant).</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But while strong build quality, image quality, and focusing do make for a powerful package, even more impressive are the lenses&#8217; compact builds. <a aria-label=\"Travel photographers (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/10-travel-photography-tips/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Travel photographers</a>, street photographers, and videographers will love the pocket-sized design, perfect for on-the-go shooting, long hours behind the camera, and international travel. In fact, all three lenses are <em>identical </em>in size, so you can pack them all without sacrificing weight or space. Check out the lenses next to one another:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-206761\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:66.67%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/sony-unveils-three-prime-lenses-1.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Sony unveils three prime lenses \" class=\"wp-image-206761\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/sony-unveils-three-prime-lenses-1.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/sony-unveils-three-prime-lenses-1.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/sony-unveils-three-prime-lenses-1.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/sony-unveils-three-prime-lenses-1.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/sony-unveils-three-prime-lenses-1.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/sony-unveils-three-prime-lenses-1.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>And the prices are surprisingly reasonable. You can grab each lens for just $600 USD &#8211; not bad at all, given the optics, build quality, and AF capabilities.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So if you&#8217;re a Sony shooter in need of a new lens (or two, or three) for travel photography, portrait photography, street photography, or handheld videography, I highly recommend you take a closer look at these options. Use the hashtag #dPSLight </strong></p>\n</p>\n<p>Light comes in MANY shapes and sizes, my first try with adding light to a photo came from a funny little desk lamp (We called it ghetto lighting) I used to stand around trying to get the ceiling light (one of those big paper ball things) in the right spot to give me the light I wanted, the addiction starting mostly on the 29th of September, 2008&#8230;</p>\n</p>\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n<figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img class=\"wp-image-206370\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/2900314972_83041980eb_k.jpg?ssl=1\" alt=\"Simon Pollock Ghetto Lighting\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n</div>\n</p>\n<p>These days <strong>lighting</strong> comes in many (as many as it always has, plus a couple more?) forms, I&#8217;ll share the ones I use &#8211; I have a single flash, it&#8217;s a Jinbei HD-2 Pro and a very capable little unit! If I need more power, and what I use on any commercial shoot, as well as the HD-2 Pro, are my two Westcott FJ-400 studio lights, they&#8217;re very nice, powerful enough for pretty much anything I need them for. Other <strong>lights</strong> I love and use often are the two little Aputure AL-MW lights (they&#8217;re waterproof) and I have two Spiffy RGB LED lights, too&#8230; A collection of many years I guess you&#8217;d say!</p>\n</p>\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n<figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img class=\"wp-image-206375\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/light.jpg?ssl=1\" alt=\"Weekly Photo Challenge â Artificial Light\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n</div>\n</p>\n<p>BUT you don&#8217;t need to have &#8220;proper lighting gear&#8221; you need to have a desire to learn and a desk lamp! SO for this week&#8217;s challenge, we want you to use ANY sort of artificial light in your photograph (Just one photograph for the challenge, folks) and share it in the comments below or via social media (Tag us!) and make sure you tag #dPSLight on social media.</p>\n</p>\n<p class=\"has-text-align-center\"><strong><a class=\"ek-link\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/challenge/weekly/\" target=\"_blank\">Missed a Challenge? It was authored by <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/author/johnmcintire/\">John McIntire</a>.</p>\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-205767\" style=\"width:1200px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1200px; padding-top:100%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1200\" height=\"1200\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/black-and-white-headshots-1001.jpg?resize=1200%2C1200&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"10 tips for beautiful black and white headshots\" class=\"wp-image-205767\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/black-and-white-headshots-1001.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/black-and-white-headshots-1001.jpg?resize=300%2C300&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/black-and-white-headshots-1001.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/black-and-white-headshots-1001.jpg?resize=150%2C150&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/black-and-white-headshots-1001.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/black-and-white-headshots-1001.jpg?resize=717%2C717&#38;ssl=1 717w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/black-and-white-headshots-1001.jpg?resize=50%2C50&#38;ssl=1 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Black and white has long been a popular way to capture headshots with impact and visual interest. The lack of color helps to emphasize the subject while discarding information that isn&#8217;t relevant.Â </p>\n\n\n\n<p>And in this article, I&#8217;m going to share 10 black and white headshot tips to help you get the best results.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let&#8217;s get started.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"headshots-vs-portraits\">Headshots vs. portraits</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202906\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:76.33%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1145\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-versus-portrait-12881288.jpg?resize=1500%2C1145&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"black and white headshots\" class=\"wp-image-202906\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-versus-portrait-12881288.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-versus-portrait-12881288.jpg?resize=300%2C229&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-versus-portrait-12881288.jpg?resize=600%2C458&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-versus-portrait-12881288.jpg?resize=768%2C586&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-versus-portrait-12881288.jpg?resize=717%2C547&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>A headshot is always a portrait, but a portrait (including a closely cropped portrait) is not always a headshot. Remember, headshots (no matter the type) come with a specific goal.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>If you&#8217;re new to <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/10-ways-to-take-stunning-portraits/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"portrait photography (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">portrait photography</a>, it might help to clear up what a headshot actually <em>is </em>before you try to create one.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Portraits</strong>:Â In general terms, a portrait photograph is a representation of a person. Portrait photography is a broad genre that encompasses nearly every subgenre that involves photographing people. It doesn&#8217;t matter if we&#8217;re talking <a aria-label=\"studio portraits (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/5-tips-setup-home-studio-dramatic-portraits/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">studio portraits</a>, <a aria-label=\"street candids (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/getting-close-and-personal-11-tips-for-close-up-candid-street-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">street candids</a>, or <a aria-label=\"fashion photography (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/10-fashion-photography-tips/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">fashion photography</a>. If it has a person in the frame, it&#8217;s probably a portrait.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Headshots</strong>: Headshots are a subgenre of portrait photography. The difference is that headshots serve a very specific purpose. Whether it&#8217;s actors&#8217; headshots or corporate headshots, the purpose is to sell something. That something could be an actor&#8217;s ability to fit a role&#8217;s physical requirements, or it could be your business professionalism.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Headshots are limited to close-up images of the subject&#8217;s head. They can also include head and shoulders as well as half-length shots. Before capturing a headshot, it&#8217;s important you understand where and how the photo will be used so you can get the right shot for the right purpose.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"tips-for-black-and-white-headshots\">Tips for black and white headshots</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202905\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:73.27%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1099\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-56835683.jpg?resize=1500%2C1099&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"black and white headshot of a man\" class=\"wp-image-202905\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-56835683.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-56835683.jpg?resize=300%2C220&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-56835683.jpg?resize=600%2C440&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-56835683.jpg?resize=768%2C563&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-56835683.jpg?resize=717%2C525&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption><a href=\"https://geni.us/Canon5DMarkIIIdPS\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Canon 5D Mark III (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Canon 5D Mark III</a> | <a href=\"https://geni.us/Canon50mmmacro\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Canon EF 50mm f/2.5 Macro (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Canon EF 50mm f/2.5 Macro</a> | 50mm | 1/80s&#160;| f/5.6 | ISO 100</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>There are no hard and fast rules for creating headshots. However, following these tips will hopefully help! </p>\n\n\n\n<p>And as always with photography, remember: There is no one way to do anything.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In other words, nothing listed here is a rule of any sort. If a tip fails to help you get the results you want or need, then discard or revamp it. &#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"remember-that-a-headshot-is-different-from-a-portrait\">1. Remember that a headshot is different from a portrait</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-default\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202903\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:75%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1125\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-vs-portrait-7698.jpg?resize=1500%2C1125&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"portrait vs headshot\" class=\"wp-image-202903\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-vs-portrait-7698.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-vs-portrait-7698.jpg?resize=300%2C225&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-vs-portrait-7698.jpg?resize=600%2C450&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-vs-portrait-7698.jpg?resize=768%2C576&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-headshot-vs-portrait-7698.jpg?resize=717%2C538&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Yes, we&#8217;ve already discussed this &#8211; but when you&#8217;re in the middle of a session, it&#8217;s easy to get caught up and start changing your approach. This may not be a problem in a normal portrait session, but with headshots, you need to make sure you&#8217;re focused on the specific end result. If you change tack and the results aren&#8217;t showing your subject in the desired manner, you&#8217;ll have wasted time and effort on images that are unsuitable for the subject&#8217;s uses.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>One way to help keep you on track is to ask your subject to share the purpose of their headshot. Allow them to be as specific and detailed as possible. Once you have an answer to that question, you should find it much easier to stay on track.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are photographing an actor with representation, ask them for their agency&#8217;s headshot guidelines (or ask the agency yourself). This will give you a strict set of limitations and help to ensure you get the required result.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"getting-it-right-in-camera-is-just-as-important-as-ever\">2. Getting it right in-camera is just as important as ever</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202902\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:75%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1125\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-sooc-1944.jpg?resize=1500%2C1125&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"black and white vs color portrait comparison\" class=\"wp-image-202902\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-sooc-1944.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-sooc-1944.jpg?resize=300%2C225&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-sooc-1944.jpg?resize=600%2C450&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-sooc-1944.jpg?resize=768%2C576&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-sooc-1944.jpg?resize=717%2C538&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>By shooting with black and white in mind and getting it right in-camera, you can help make the conversion process much easier. <br />Canon 5D Mark III | Canon EF 50mm f/2.5 Macro | 50mm | 1/125s | f/5.6 | ISO 100</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Depending on where your headshots are going to wind up, you might find that you can&#8217;t do any edits beyond <a aria-label=\"basic retouching (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/5-must-know-photoshop-retouching-tips-tricks-photographers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">basic retouching</a>. You should be allowed a <a aria-label=\"black and white conversion (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/a-guide-to-black-and-white-conversion-in-lightroom/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">black and white conversion</a> and some basic <a aria-label=\"blemish removal (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/fixing-blemishes-in-lightroom/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">blemish removal</a>, but much more than that might not be acceptable.Â </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Therefore, do whatever you can to get your images right in the camera. Light your images well with good exposure and good contrast. Learn your lighting patterns and use a meter if you have to.Â </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Get this step right, and you might find that you have little more editing to do beyond the actual black and white conversion.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"start-in-color\">3. Start in color</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>It might be tempting to set your camera to a black and white mode at the point of shooting. You can do this &#8211; but if you shoot JPEGs, I would advise against it. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>By choosing this route, you will be discarding a huge amount of color information at the very beginning. For the best conversions, you&#8217;ll want to later manipulate your color information to get the very best black and white results.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>(However, note that RAW shooters can use a black and white mode while still retaining color information.)Â </p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"avoid-shooting-to-crop\">4. Avoid shooting to crop</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202901\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:57.13%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"857\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-crop.jpg?resize=1500%2C857&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"cropped portrait\" class=\"wp-image-202901\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-crop.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-crop.jpg?resize=300%2C171&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-crop.jpg?resize=600%2C343&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-crop.jpg?resize=768%2C439&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-crop.jpg?resize=339%2C194&#38;ssl=1 339w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-crop.jpg?resize=717%2C410&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>By cropping down to a head-and-shoulders composition, you discard most of the information in the frame. Instead, try to get your compositions right at the shooting stage.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This might be controversial, but I&#8217;ll stand by it. When you are creating black and white headshots, try to get your composition as close as possible to how you want it to end up. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Doing this will ensure that your images are as big as possible and have as much detail as possible when you pass them on to your client. If you shoot before cropping out significant parts of your image, you will lose out on a large chunk of resolution.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"control-contrast-with-light-not-post-production\">5. Control contrast with light, not post-production</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202900\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:66.67%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-contrast-2107.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"woman in the studio\" class=\"wp-image-202900\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-contrast-2107.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-contrast-2107.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-contrast-2107.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-contrast-2107.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-contrast-2107.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-contrast-2107.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>Using a medium-sized octabox up close allows for extremely soft light, thus controlling the contrast. Also, at camera right, you see a background light that reduces the overall contrast in the image.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This point goes back to getting it right in-camera, but specifically for lighting. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>One of the quickest ways to ruin a portrait is to add a lot of unnatural contrast in the post-production phase. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Avoid this by setting up your lights to get the contrast you want from the very start.Â </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can do this through <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/a-beginners-guide-to-light-modifiers/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"modifier selection (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">modifier selection</a> and <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/lighting-ratios-to-make-or-break-your-portrait/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"lighting ratios (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">lighting ratios</a>.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"use-fill-to-control-your-contrast\">6. Use fill to control your contrast</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202899\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:75%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1125\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-fill-5029.jpg?resize=1500%2C1125&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"headshot with and without fill light\" class=\"wp-image-202899\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-fill-5029.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-fill-5029.jpg?resize=300%2C225&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-fill-5029.jpg?resize=600%2C450&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-fill-5029.jpg?resize=768%2C576&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-fill-5029.jpg?resize=717%2C538&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>Left: Without fill. Right: With fill. Here you can see how a fill light might help you lift the shadows and control the contrast in your images.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>If you want to decrease contrast, make sure to do it in-camera. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can do this with <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/fill-light-in-portrait-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">fill light</a>. Whether you work with a dedicated second light source or a reflector, introducing fill into your images is a great way to control exactly how your black and white headshots turn out.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"think-in-values-rather-than-color\">7. Think in values rather than color</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202908\" style=\"width:1148px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1148px; padding-top:130.66%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1148\" height=\"1500\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-value-74767476.jpg?resize=1148%2C1500&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"black and white headshot of a woman\" class=\"wp-image-202908\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-value-74767476.jpg?w=1148&#38;ssl=1 1148w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-value-74767476.jpg?resize=230%2C300&#38;ssl=1 230w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-value-74767476.jpg?resize=459%2C600&#38;ssl=1 459w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-value-74767476.jpg?resize=768%2C1003&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-value-74767476.jpg?resize=717%2C937&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>In this image, you can see four distinct areas of value: The highlights of the skin, the midtones of the sweater, and two shadow areas for the hair and the background. Being able to see these at the time of shooting will help you design your black and white headshots better. <br />Canon 5D Mark III | Canon EF 50mm f/2.5 Macro | 50mm | 1/160 secÂ | f/4 | ISO 100</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Because you are starting in color, it can help to think of things in terms of values. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>At its most basic, <em>value </em>simply describes where colors fall on a spectrum between pure white and pure black. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, once converted to black and white, almost everything in your images will appear as a shade of gray. If you can visualize how the colors you see with your eyes will be represented in a black and white conversion, you will be better able to design your lighting before your subject even arrives.Â </p>\n\n\n\n<p>How do you learn to do this? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Practice. A lot of it. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Get out there and photograph anything and everything you can, then convert to black and white so you can build this skill. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Remember, different conversion techniques affect color and value in different ways, so be sure to practice with as many conversion methods as possible.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"minimize-details-in-the-frame\">8. Minimize details in the frame</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Because we are talking about headshots, you&#8217;ll need to remember that the entire point of the photograph is the person. Any extra details will only serve to detract from your subject. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>So do what you can to minimize the impact of the background, the subject&#8217;s clothing, and other elements in the photo.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For backgrounds, you can focus your efforts on finding the cleanest, most non-distracting backdrop. For clothing, ask your subjects to dress without distracting elements that would take the focus off of them. Patterns can be fine, but it might be best if you avoided particularly bold choices like leopard-print and zebra-stripe tops.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"focus-on-form\">9. Focus on form</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202898\" style=\"width:1000px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1000px; padding-top:150%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1500\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-shape-1823.jpg?resize=1000%2C1500&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"black and white headshot of a woman\" class=\"wp-image-202898\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-shape-1823.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-shape-1823.jpg?resize=200%2C300&#38;ssl=1 200w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-shape-1823.jpg?resize=400%2C600&#38;ssl=1 400w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-shape-1823.jpg?resize=768%2C1152&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-shape-1823.jpg?resize=717%2C1076&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>When you are lighting your subject, take the time to ensure that you&#8217;re using the light to shape their features in the best way possible. <br />Canon 5D Mark III | Canon EF 50mm f/2.5 Macro | 50mm | 1/100s&#160;| f/9 | ISO 100</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This goes back to basic lighting skills.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You need to shape your subject&#8217;s face in a flattering way that also helps it stand out in the frame. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You are trying to minimize other details, so it is the subject&#8217;s features you must focus on. Make as much use of them as you can.Â </p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"eyes-and-expressions-are-more-important-than-ever\">10. Eyes and expressions are more important than ever</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image caption-align-left is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202897\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:50%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"750\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-expressions-1029.jpg?resize=1500%2C750&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"black and white headshot examples\" class=\"wp-image-202897\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-expressions-1029.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-expressions-1029.jpg?resize=300%2C150&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-expressions-1029.jpg?resize=600%2C300&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-expressions-1029.jpg?resize=768%2C384&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-expressions-1029.jpg?resize=717%2C359&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span><figcaption>With headshots, expressions and eye contact are more important than ever. Do what you can to develop a rapport with your subjects.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>As the goal of a headshot is to make your subject look as good as possible, and as you have already reduced the impact of distracting elements, your subject&#8217;s <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/3-simple-ways-create-stunning-eyes-portrait-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">eyes</a> and <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/poser-achieve-perfect-portrait-expression/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">expression</a> become more important than ever.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Lighting for the eyes will keep them bright and prominent in the frame. Doing this also means you won&#8217;t have to spend time processing the eyes, which might work well for your client&#8217;s requirements.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Also, to get the best expressions, ensure that your subject is comfortable and that you have a good rapport with them.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"black-and-white-headshots-not-the-end\">Black and white headshots: (not) the end</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>On their own, headshot photography and black and white photography are broad topics that are truly impossible to distill into a short list of tips. However, I do hope that these ten tips for black and white headshots will help you get started on your journey. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>As always, none of these tips are rules, just guidance. If you feel that something I said doesn&#8217;t suit you or your photography, that&#8217;s perfectly fine.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now over to you:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>Which of these black and white headshot tips did you like the most? Do you have any tips for black and white headshot photography? Share your thoughts (and photos) in the comments below!</em></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-default\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><span class=\"responsive-image wp-image-202907\" style=\"width:1500px\"><span class=\"space\" style=\"width:1500px; padding-top:50%\"></span><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"750\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-top-7698.jpg?resize=1500%2C750&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Tips for better black and white headshots.\" class=\"wp-image-202907\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-top-7698.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-top-7698.jpg?resize=300%2C150&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-top-7698.jpg?resize=600%2C300&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-top-7698.jpg?resize=768%2C384&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-top-7698.jpg?resize=717%2C359&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></span></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"schema-faq wp-block-yoast-faq-block\"><div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1612132238314\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">Should I shoot headshots in black and white mode?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">If you&#8217;re shooting in JPEG, no. But if you&#8217;re shooting in RAW, you can decide whether to shoot in black and white or color (you won&#8217;t lose any image information in either mode).</p> </div> <div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1612132418003\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">Is black and white a good option for headshots?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">Yes. Black and white allows you to strip down the information in the photo to its key elements (in this case, the person whose headshot it is).</p> </div> <div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1612132491547\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">What kind of light should I use for headshots?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">Any soft light that flatters your subject is a good choice.</p> </div> <div class=\"schema-faq-section\" id=\"faq-question-1612132537922\"><strong class=\"schema-faq-question\">How should I do black and white conversions for my headshot photography?</strong> <p class=\"schema-faq-answer\">Use whatever method suits you and your workflow best. Photoshop and Lightroom both offer great options for black and white conversions.</p> </div> </div>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/black-and-white-headshots/\">10 Tips for Beautiful Black and White Headshots</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>. 9b.webp","https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-value-74767476.jpg?resize=1148%2C1500&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn55@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-49-38-256_264d5180b54d4d9c.webp","https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-shape-1823.jpg?resize=1000%2C1500&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn55@2020_4/2021/04/03/04-49-40-054_1e2ddf76c6236bdb.webp","https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-expressions-1029.jpg?resize=1500%2C750&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn46@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-49-37-131_7f301bba677b489b.webp","https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/black-and-white-headshots-top-7698.jpg?resize=1500%2C750&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-49-38-269_111a763da345b279.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/DigitalPhotographySchool?i=FHlM1g5HXuc:8qicBZA_mrM:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn9@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-49-37-375_e4147166174c2223.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/DigitalPhotographySchool?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn31@2020_1/2021/04/03/04-49-39-839_849a6e90690e7208.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/DigitalPhotographySchool?d=ByNYXvuKCJE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn34@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-49-37-112_7752f86734b1d8c8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/DigitalPhotographySchool?i=FHlM1g5HXuc:8qicBZA_mrM:guobEISWfyQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn75@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-49-37-137_5ac67e0700a44e4e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/DigitalPhotographySchool/~4/FHlM1g5HXuc":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn15@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-49-37-318_450e2c5dfc918c46.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425373900},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/lighting-ratios-to-make-or-break-your-portrait/\">A Lighting Ratios Guide: How to Make (or Break) Your Portraits</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>. It was authored by <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/author/darlene-hildebrandt/\">Darlene Hildebrandt</a>.</p>\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure
